<p><b>Bridgeport</b> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Connecticut" title="List of cities in Connecticut">largest city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>. Located in <a href="/wiki/Fairfield_County,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield County, Connecticut">Fairfield County</a> at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Pequonnock_River" title="Pequonnock River">Pequonnock River</a> on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a>, the city had a population of 144,229 during the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2010_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-4">[4]</a></sup> making it also the 5th-most populous in <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> It is bordered by the towns of <a href="/wiki/Trumbull,_Connecticut" title="Trumbull, Connecticut">Trumbull</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield, Connecticut">Fairfield</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Stratford,_Connecticut" title="Stratford, Connecticut">Stratford</a> to the east. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Bridgeport" title="Greater Bridgeport">Greater Bridgeport</a> area is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_urban_areas" title="List of United States urban areas">48th-largest urban area in the United States</a> and forms part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York-Newark-Bridgeport,_NY-NJ-CT-PA_CSA" title="New York-Newark-Bridgeport, NY-NJ-CT-PA CSA">Greater New York City Area</a>.</p>
<p>Bridgeport was inhabited by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paugussett" title="Paugussett">Paugussett</a> <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Indian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_tribes" title="Native American tribes">tribe</a> at the time of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="English colonization of the Americas">English colonization</a>. The English farming community became a center of trade, shipbuilding, and whaling. The town incorporated itself to subsidize the <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_Railroad" title="Housatonic Railroad">Housatonic Railroad</a> and rapidly industrialized following its connection to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Haven_Railroad" title="New York and New Haven Railroad">New York and New Haven</a> railroad. Manufacturing was the mainstay of the local economy until the 1970s. Industrial restructuring and suburbanization caused the loss of many jobs and affluent residents, leaving Bridgeport struggling with problems of poverty and crime. In the 21st century, conversion of office and factory buildings to residential use and other redevelopment is attracting new residents.</p>
<p>The showman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.T._Barnum" title="P.T. Barnum">P.T. Barnum</a> was a resident of the city and served as the town's mayor in the late 19th century. Barnum built four houses in Bridgeport, and housed his circus in town during winter. The first <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a> restaurant opened in the North End section of the city in 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Frisbie_Pie_Company" title="Frisbie Pie Company">Frisbie Pie Company</a> was located here, and Bridgeport is credited as the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Frisbee" title="Frisbee">Frisbee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="History of Bridgeport, Connecticut">History of Bridgeport, Connecticut</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_history">Colonial history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Stratfield_(Bridgeport)_Map_before_1886.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2267" data-file-width="1851" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg/200px-Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg/300px-Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg/400px-Old_Stratfield_%28Bridgeport%29_Map_before_1886.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Stratfield_(Bridgeport)_Map_before_1886.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Colonial Stratfield</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first documented <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> settlement within the present city limits of Bridgeport took place in 1644, centered at Black Rock Harbor along North Avenue and between Park and Briarwood Avenues. The place was called <b>Pequonnock</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Quiripi_language" title="Quiripi language">Quiripi</a> for "Cleared Land"), after a band of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paugussett" title="Paugussett">Paugussett</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> people who then occupied this area. One of their sacred sites was Golden Hill, which overlooked the harbor and was the location of natural springs and their planting fields. (It has since been blasted through for an expressway.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._14.E2.80.9316_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._14.E2.80.9316-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Americana_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Americana-10">[10]</a></sup> The Golden Hill Indians were granted a <a href="/wiki/Indian_reservation" title="Indian reservation">reservation</a> here by the <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">Colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Colony" title="Connecticut Colony">Connecticut</a> in 1639 that survived until 1802. (It exists today in adjoining <a href="/wiki/Trumbull,_Connecticut" title="Trumbull, Connecticut">Trumbull</a>.)</p>
<p>Bridgeport's early years were marked by residents' reliance on <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">farming</a>, not altogether different from the economy of the Native Americans, who had cultivated <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, beans, and squash and fished and gathered shellfish from both the river and sound. A village called <b>Newfield</b> began to coalesce around the corner of State and Water Streets in the 1760s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609-11">[11]</a></sup> The area officially became known as <b>Stratfield</b> in 1695<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> or 1701 due to its location between the already existing towns of <i>Strat</i>ford and Fair<i>field</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_pp._470.E2.80.93474_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_pp._470.E2.80.93474-12">[12]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, Newfield Harbor was a center of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privateering" title="Privateering">privateering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EA.27.271918_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EA.27.271918-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iranistan,_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum,_1848.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2567" data-file-width="3629" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg/200px-Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg/300px-Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg/400px-Iranistan%2C_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum%2C_1848.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iranistan,_Residence_of_P.T._Barnum,_1848.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Iranistan" title="Iranistan">Iranistan</a>, the residence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.T._Barnum" title="P.T. Barnum">P.T. Barnum</a>, in 1848</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport_1824.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2762" data-file-width="3450" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Bridgeport_1824.png/200px-Bridgeport_1824.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Bridgeport_1824.png/300px-Bridgeport_1824.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Bridgeport_1824.png/400px-Bridgeport_1824.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport_1824.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bridgeport in 1824, by <span class="nowrap">H. L.</span> Barnum<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_endpaper_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_endpaper-14">[14]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1845_NY%26NH.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4718" data-file-width="29026" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/1845_NY%26NH.jpg/200px-1845_NY%26NH.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/1845_NY%26NH.jpg/300px-1845_NY%26NH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/1845_NY%26NH.jpg/400px-1845_NY%26NH.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1845_NY%26NH.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The route of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NY%26NH" title="NY&amp;NH">NY&amp;NH</a>, showing Bridgeport in 1845</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River,_by_Whitney,_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="883" data-file-width="1134" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg/220px-East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg/330px-East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg/440px-East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River%2C_by_Whitney%2C_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:East_Bridgeport_Bridge_over_Pequannock_River,_by_Whitney,_Beckwith_%26_Paradice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
East Bridgeport Bridge over Pequannock River, ca. 1850</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_(United_States)" title="State (United States)">State</a> of <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>'s ratification of the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States" title="Constitution of the United States">constitution</a> in 1781, many of the local farmers held shares in vessels trading at Newfield Harbor or had begun trading in their own name. Newfield initially expanded around the coasting trade with <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> and the international trade with the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._222.E2.80.935_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._222.E2.80.935-15">[15]</a></sup> The commercial activity of the village was clustered around the wharves on the west bank of the Pequonnock, while the churches were erected inland on Broad Street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_endpaper_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_endpaper-14">[14]</a></sup> In 1800, the village became the <a href="/wiki/Borough_(Connecticut)" title="Borough (Connecticut)">Borough</a> of Bridgeport,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> the first so <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._588_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._588-19">[19]</a></sup> It was named for the Newfield or Lottery Bridge across the Pequonnock, connecting the wharves on its east and west banks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-puslastac_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-puslastac-17">[17]</a></sup> Bridgeport Bank was established in 1806.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._597_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._597-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1821, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Townships_in_the_United_States" title="Townships in the United States">township</a> of Bridgeport became independent of Stratford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The West India trade died down around 1840,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609-11">[11]</a></sup> but by that time the Bridgeport <a href="/wiki/History_of_steamship_lines" title="History of steamship lines">Steamship</a> Company (1824)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._610_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._610-22">[22]</a></sup> and Bridgeport <a href="/wiki/History_of_whaling" title="History of whaling">Whaling</a> Company (1833) had been incorporated<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._I.2C_p._609-11">[11]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_Railroad" title="Housatonic Railroad">Housatonic Railroad</a> chartered (1836).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._695_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._695-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-choochoo_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-choochoo-24">[24]</a></sup> The HRRC ran upstate along the <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_River" title="Housatonic River">Housatonic Valley</a>, connecting with <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berkshire_Railroad" title="Berkshire Railroad">Berkshire Railroad</a> at the state line. Bridgeport was chartered as Connecticut's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Connecticut" title="List of cities in Connecticut">fifth city</a> in 1836<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._37.E2.80.9338_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_pp._37.E2.80.9338-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> in order to enable the town council to secure funding (ultimately <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">$</a>150,000) to provide to the HRRC and ensure that it would terminate in Bridgeport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._696_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._696-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Naugatuck_Railroad" title="Naugatuck Railroad">Naugatuck Railroad</a>—connecting Bridgeport to <a href="/wiki/Waterbury,_Connecticut" title="Waterbury, Connecticut">Waterbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winsted,_Connecticut" title="Winsted, Connecticut">Winsted</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Naugatuck_River" title="Naugatuck River">Naugatuck</a>—was chartered in 1845 and began operation four years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._698.E2.80.939_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._698.E2.80.939-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gochoochoo_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-gochoochoo-31">[31]</a></sup> The same year, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Haven_Railroad" title="New York and New Haven Railroad">New York and New Haven Railroad</a> began operation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._703_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrcutt1886Vol._II.2C_p._703-32">[32]</a></sup> connecting Bridgeport to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> and the other towns along the north shore of the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a>.</p>
<p>Now a major junction for western Connecticut, the city rapidly industrialized. Following the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>, it held several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_founding" title="Iron founding">iron foundries</a> and factories manufacturing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firearm_industry" title="Firearm industry">firearms</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metallic_cartridge" title="Metallic cartridge">metallic cartridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_harness" title="Horse harness">horse harnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lock_(security_device)" title="Lock (security device)">locks</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blinds" title="Blinds">blinds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271878-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wheeler_%26_Wilson" title="Wheeler &amp; Wilson">Wheeler &amp; Wilson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sewing_machine" title="Sewing machine">sewing machines</a> were exported throughout the world. Bridgeport annexed the West End and the village of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Rock_(Bridgeport)" title="Black Rock (Bridgeport)">Black Rock</a> and its busy <a href="/wiki/Black_Rock_Harbor" title="Black Rock Harbor">harbor</a> in 1870.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1875, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.T._Barnum" title="P.T. Barnum">P.T. Barnum</a> was elected mayor of the town, which afterwards served as the winter headquarters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barnum_and_Bailey%27s_Circus" title="Barnum and Bailey's Circus">Barnum and Bailey's Circus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bill%27s_Wild_West_Show" title="Buffalo Bill's Wild West Show">Buffalo Bill's Wild West Show</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="969" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg/200px-PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg/300px-PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg/400px-PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PostcardBridgeportCTMainSt1912.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1912 postcard showing Main Street in Bridgeport</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1024" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg/200px-BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg/300px-BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg/400px-BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BridgeportCT_SterlingBlockBishopArcade_Inside.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sterling Block-Bishop Arcade, a Victorian-era <a href="/wiki/Arcade_(architecture)" title="Arcade (architecture)">shopping arcade</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1870 to 1910, Bridgeport became the major industrial center of Connecticut and its population rose from around 25,000 to over 100,000, including thousands of <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Americans" title="Slovak Americans">Slovaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Americans" title="Hungarian Americans">Hungarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">Italian immigrants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singer_Manufacturing_Company" title="Singer Manufacturing Company">Singer</a> factory joined Wheeler &amp; Wilson in producing sewing machines<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Locomobile_Company_of_America" title="Locomobile Company of America">Locomobile Company of America</a> was a prominent early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" title="Automobile manufacturer">automobile manufacturer</a>, producing a prototype of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanley_Steamer" title="Stanley Steamer">Stanley Steamer</a> and various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luxury_car" title="Luxury car">luxury cars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The town was the center of America's <a href="/wiki/Corset" title="Corset">corset</a> production, responsible for almost 20% of the national total,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> and became the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Remington_Arms" title="Remington Arms">Remington Arms</a> following its 1912 merger with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Metallic_Cartridge_Co." title="Union Metallic Cartridge Co.">Union Metallic Cartridge Co.</a> Around the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, Bridgeport was also producing steam-fitting and heating apparatuses, brass goods, <a href="/wiki/Phonograph" title="Phonograph">phonographs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typewriter" title="Typewriter">typewriters</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911_8-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.271911-8">[8]</a></sup> milling machines, <a href="/wiki/Bra" title="Bra">brassieres</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saddle" title="Saddle">saddles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>A series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_strike" title="Labor strike">strikes</a> in the summer of 1915 imposed the <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour day</a> on the town's factories; rather than moving business elsewhere, the success spread the eight-hour day throughout the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_United_States" title="Northeast United States">Northeast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> continued the city's expansion so that, on the eve of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, there were more than 500 factories in Bridgeport, including <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a>' primary pressing plant. The build-up to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> helped its recovery in the late 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Restructuring of heavy industry starting after the mid-20th century caused the loss of thousands of jobs and residents. Like other urban centers in Connecticut, Bridgeport suffered during the <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">deindustrialization</a> of the United States in the 1970s and 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Continued development of new suburban housing attracted middle and upper-class residents, leaving the city with a higher proportion of poor. The city suffered from overall mismanagement, for which several city officials were convicted, contributing to the economic and social decline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times_dc_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-times_dc-39">[39]</a></sup> In September 1978, Bridgeport teachers went on a 19-day strike due to deadlocked contract negotiations. A court order, as well as a state law that made strikes by public workers illegal in Connecticut, resulted in 274 teachers being arrested and jailed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Bridgeport made numerous efforts at revitalization. In one proposal, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a> developer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steve_Wynn_(developer)" title="Steve Wynn (developer)">Steve Wynn</a> was to build a large <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a>, but that project failed. In 1991, the city filed for <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a> protection but was declared solvent by a federal court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="500" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg/200px-Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg/300px-Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg/400px-Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport_101_0153small.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A street scene in Bridgeport</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 21st century, Bridgeport has taken steps toward redevelopment of its downtown and other neighborhoods. In 2004, artists' lofts were developed in the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Read%27s_Department_Store" title="Read's Department Store">Read's Department Store</a> on Broad Street. Several other rental conversions have been completed, including the 117-unit Citytrust bank building on Main Street. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_recession" title="2008 recession">recession</a> halted, at least temporarily, two major mixed-use projects including a $1-billion waterfront development at Steel Point, but other redevelopment projects have proceeded, such as the condominium conversion project in Bijou Square.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2009, the City Council approved a new master plan for development, designed both to promote redevelopment in selected areas and to protect existing residential neighborhoods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2010, the Bridgeport Housing Authority and a local health center announced plans to build a $20 million medical and housing complex at Albion Street, making use of federal stimulus funds and designed to replace some of the housing lost with the demolition of <a href="/wiki/Father_Panik_Village" title="Father Panik Village">Father Panik Village</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_speeches">Notable speeches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Notable speeches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 10, 1860, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> spoke in the city's Washington Hall, an auditorium at the old <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_City_Hall" title="Bridgeport City Hall">Bridgeport City Hall</a> (now McLevy Hall), at the corner of State and Broad Streets. The largest room in the city was packed, and a crowd formed outside, as well. Lincoln received a standing ovation before taking the 9:07 pm train that night back to Manhattan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burr_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-burr-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> A plaque marks the site where Lincoln spoke; later that year, he was elected president.</p>
<p>The Rev. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> spoke three times at the Klein Auditorium during the 1960s. Additionally, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> spoke before a small group of Connecticut business people and officials at the Playhouse on the Green in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> also spoke at the Harbor Yard arena in 2010 to gain support for the campaign of Democratic Governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dan_Malloy" title="Dan Malloy">Dan Malloy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="Geography of Bridgeport, Connecticut">Geography of Bridgeport, Connecticut</a></div>
<p>Bridgeport is located along <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a> at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Pequonnock_River" title="Pequonnock River">Pequonnock River</a>, named for the Native American tribe who historically lived along it.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport is renowned for its public park system, which has led to its official nickname as "The Park City". The city's first public park was the westerly portion of McLevy Green, first set aside as a public square 1806,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_p._277_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_p._277-49">[49]</a></sup> although the Clinton Park Militia Grounds (1666) and Old Mill Green (1717) were set aside earlier as public commons by the towns of Fairfield and Stratford, respectively. As the city rapidly grew in population, residents recognized the need for more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_parks" title="Public parks">public parks</a> and by 1864, Barnum and other residents had donated approximately 44 acres (180,000 m<sup>2</sup>) to create <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaside_Park_(Bridgeport,_Connecticut)" title="Seaside Park (Bridgeport, Connecticut)">Seaside Park</a>, now increased by acquisition and landfill to 375 acres (1.52 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time2002_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-time2002-50">[50]</a></sup> In 1878, over 100 acres (400,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of land bordering the <a href="/wiki/Pequonnock_River" title="Pequonnock River">Pequonnock River</a> was added as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beardsley_Park" title="Beardsley Park">Beardsley Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_p._280_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldo1917Vol._I.2C_p._280-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a>, famous for creating New York City's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>, designed both Seaside and Beardsley Parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olmsted_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-olmsted-52">[52]</a></sup> Over time, more parks were added including 35-acre (140,000 m<sup>2</sup>) Beechwood Park and <a href="/wiki/Pleasure_Beach" title="Pleasure Beach">Pleasure Beach</a>, home to a popular amusement park for many years.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city of Bridgeport is divided into many distinct neighborhoods,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> divided into five geographic areas: Downtown, the East Side, the North End, the South End, and the West Side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Downtown</b>
<ul>
<li>McLeevy Green</li>
<li>Harral Square</li>
<li>The Hollow</li>
<li>Enterprise Zone</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>East Side</b>
<ul>
<li>Boston Avenue/Mill Hill</li>
<li>East End</li>
<li>Lower East Side</li>
<li>Newfield</li>
<li>Pleasure Beach</li>
<li>Steel Point</li>
<li>Upper East Side</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>North End</b>
<ul>
<li>Brooklawn/St. Vincent</li>
<li>Lake Forest</li>
<li>Lake Success</li>
<li>North Bridgeport/Little Italy</li>
<li>Reservoir/Whiskey Hill</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>South End</b>
<ul>
<li>Seaside Park</li>
<li>Soundgate</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>West Side</b>
<ul>
<li>Black Rock</li>
<li>West End</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, Bridgeport straddles between a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a> (<i>Cfa</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental</a> (<i>Dfa</i>) climate, with some maritime influence; it is part of USDA <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zone</a> 7a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The normal average monthly temperature ranges from 30.1 °F (−1.1 °C) in January to 74.3 °F (23.5 °C) in July; on average, there are 20 days where the temperature remains at or below freezing and 7.6 days with a high at or above 90 °F (32 °C) annually; the last year to not reach the latter mark was 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-56">[56]</a></sup> Temperatures reaching 0 °F (−18 °C) or 100 °F (38 °C) are rare, and were last seen respectively on February 14, 2016 and July 22, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-56">[56]</a></sup> The record low is −7 °F (−22 °C), set on January 22, 1984, while the record high is 103 °F (39 °C), set on July 22 in 1957 and 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Precipitation averages 42.7 inches (1,080 mm) annually, and is somewhat evenly distributed throughout the year, though March and April are the wettest months in terms of total precipitation. Snowfall averages 27.6 inches (70 cm) per winter, falling almost entirely from December to March. As is typical of coastal Connecticut, snow cover does not usually remain for long, with an average of 29 days per winter with snow cover of at least 1 inch (2.5 cm).</p>

<td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">Population 1840–1970<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><br/>
U.S. Decennial Census<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><br/>
2014 Estimate<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCensusEst2014_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCensusEst2014-61">[61]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of 2000, there were 139,529 people, 50,307 households, and 32,749 families residing in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 8,720.9 people per square mile (3,367.0/km²). There were 54,367 housing units at an average density of 3,398.1 per square mile (1,312.0/km²). The racial makeup of the city was 45.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 30.8% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 0.5% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 3.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 20.3% of the population. Other ancestry groups include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> (8.6%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> (5.1%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_American" title="Portuguese American">Portuguese</a> (2.9%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">Polish</a> (2.8%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> (2.4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, there were 144,229 people residing in the city. The racial makeup of the city residents was 39.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a>; 34.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a> or African American; 3.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>; and 4.3% from two or more races. A total of 18.1% of the population were <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino of any race.</p>
<p>There were 50,307 households out of which 34.3% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 35.0% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 24.0% had a female householder with no husband present, and 34.9% were non-families. 29.0% of all households were made up of individuals and 11.3% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.70 and the average family size was 3.34.</p>
<p>In the city the population was spread out with 28.4% under the age of 18, 11.2% from 18 to 24, 30.5% from 25 to 44, 18.4% from 45 to 64, and 11.5% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 31 years. For every 100 females there were 91.2 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 86.3 males.</p>
<p>The median income for a household in the city was $34,658, and the median income for a family was $39,571. Males had a median income of $32,430 versus $26,966 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the city was $16,306. About 16.2% of families and 18.4% of the population were below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, including 24.8% of those under age 18 and 13.2% of those age 65 or over. Since 1849, <a class="external text" href="http://www.fswinc.org/" rel="nofollow">FSWINC</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/501(c)(3)_nonprofit_organization" title="501(c)(3) nonprofit organization">501(c)(3) nonprofit organization</a> has provided care for individuals living in difficult socioeconomic situations in both Bridgeport and Fairfield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to 2010 census data, the Bridgeport MSA, containing all of Fairfield County, is the most economically unequal region in America, with 57% of the wealth going to the top percentile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since the decline of its industrial sector beginning in the middle of the 20th century, Bridgeport has gradually adjusted to a service-based economy. Though a level of industrial activity continues, healthcare, finance, and education have evolved into the centerpieces of Bridgeport's economy.</p>
<p>The two largest employers within the city are Bridgeport's primary hospitals, <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Hospital" title="Bridgeport Hospital">Bridgeport Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent%27s_Medical_Center_(Bridgeport)" title="St. Vincent's Medical Center (Bridgeport)">St. Vincent's Medical Center</a>. The former Park City Hospital closed in 1993 and was reopened in 2010 as elderly and homeless housing units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Emergency medical services are provided by <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Response" title="American Medical Response">American Medical Response</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">paramedic</a> level.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bridgeport,_Connecticut" title="Education in Bridgeport, Connecticut">Education in Bridgeport, Connecticut</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bridgeport" title="University of Bridgeport">University of Bridgeport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_Community_College" title="Housatonic Community College">Housatonic Community College</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent%27s_Medical_Center_(Bridgeport)#St._Vincent.27s_College" title="St. Vincent's Medical Center (Bridgeport)">St. Vincent's College</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva_Gedola_of_Bridgeport" title="Yeshiva Gedola of Bridgeport">Yeshiva Gedola of Bridgeport</a>. The Yeshiva Gedola is currently the home of the Bridgeport Community Kollel, a rabbinic fellowship program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Bridgeport's Ernest C. Trefz School of Business offers programs for both undergraduate and graduate.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_education">Public education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Public education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's public school system has 30 elementary schools, three comprehensive high schools, two alternative programs and an interdistrict vocational aquaculture school. The system has about 20,800 students, making the Bridgeport Public Schools the second largest school system in Connecticut after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartford" title="Hartford">Hartford</a>. It is ranked #158 out of the 164 Connecticut school districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The school system employs a professional staff of more than 1,700.</p>
<p>The city has started a large school renovation and construction program, with plans for new schools and modernization of existing buildings.</p>
<p><b>Public high schools</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bassick_High_School" title="Bassick High School">Bassick High School</a> established in 1929.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_High_School_(Connecticut)" title="Central High School (Connecticut)">Central High School</a> established in 1876, home to Central Magnet, largest of the high schools.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warren_Harding_High_School" title="Warren Harding High School">Warren Harding High School</a> home to the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> Program (IBO) and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Health_Magnet_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Health Magnet Program (page does not exist)">Health Magnet Program</a> in association with Bridgeport Hospital, St. Vincent's Medical Center, and Bridgeport Manor.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport_Regional_Vocational_Aquaculture_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bridgeport Regional Vocational Aquaculture School (page does not exist)">Bridgeport Regional Vocational Aquaculture School</a> (BRVAS), a school specializing in marine and aquaculture curriculum. Located near historic Captain's Cove and open to students from surrounding towns.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bullard_Havens_Technical_High_School" title="Bullard Havens Technical High School">Bullard Havens Technical High School</a>, a vocational high school. (State School)</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bridge_Academy:_Bridgeport_Charter_High_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Bridge Academy: Bridgeport Charter High School (page does not exist)">The Bridge Academy: Bridgeport Charter High School</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Achievement_First_Bridgeport_Charter_High_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Achievement First Bridgeport Charter High School (page does not exist)">Achievement First Bridgeport Charter High School</a></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Public magnet schools</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Wheeler_Interdistrict_Multi-Magnet_High_School" title="Fairchild Wheeler Interdistrict Multi-Magnet High School">Fairchild Wheeler Interdistrict Multi-Magnet High School</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_education">Private education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Private education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport is also home to private schools, including <a class="external text" href="http://www.bridgeporthopeschool.org/" rel="nofollow">Bridgeport Hope School</a> (K-8), <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_International_Academy" title="Bridgeport International Academy">Bridgeport International Academy</a> (grades 9-12), Catholic Academies of Bridgeport (PK-8), <a href="/wiki/Kolbe_Cathedral_High_School" title="Kolbe Cathedral High School">Kolbe Cathedral High School</a> (9-12), St. Andrew Academy (PK-8), St. Ann Academy (PK-8), and Zion Lutheran School (PK-8).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BridgeportCityHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="750" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/BridgeportCityHall.jpg/220px-BridgeportCityHall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/BridgeportCityHall.jpg/330px-BridgeportCityHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/BridgeportCityHall.jpg/440px-BridgeportCityHall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BridgeportCityHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bridgeport City Hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is governed by the mayor council system. Twenty members of the city council are elected from districts. Each district elects two members. The mayor is elected by the entire city.</p>
<p>Bridgeport is notable for having had a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_America" title="Socialist Party of America">Socialist</a> mayor for 24 years; <a href="/wiki/Jasper_McLevy" title="Jasper McLevy">Jasper McLevy</a> served as mayor from 1933 to 1957. A more recent mayor, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Ganim" title="Joseph P. Ganim">Joseph P. Ganim</a>, was involved in a corruption scandal, as has been the case with some other mayors in Connecticut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In June 2006, Mayor <a href="/wiki/John_M._Fabrizi" title="John M. Fabrizi">John M. Fabrizi</a> admitted that he had used <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> while in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxes">Taxes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Taxes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Taxes are high in Bridgeport, and the second highest in the county. In 2005, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mill_rate" title="Mill rate">mill rate</a> for Bridgeport was 42.28<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and is reportedly 41.855 for fiscal year 2013-2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barnum_Museum,_Bridgeport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="880" data-file-width="768" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg/220px-Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg/330px-Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg/440px-Barnum_Museum%2C_Bridgeport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Theater_and_music">Theater and music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Theater and music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bridgeport has a number of venues for live theater and music events, ranging from intimate performing spaces to a stadium hosting rock concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globe2008_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-globe2008-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Downtown Cabaret Theatre – cabaret, children's theater, concerts</li>
<li>Playhouse on the Green – (228 seats) theater with plays and varied musical events</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Klein_Memorial_Auditorium" title="Klein Memorial Auditorium">Klein Memorial Auditorium</a> – (1,400 seats) home to the Greater Bridgeport Symphony, touring shows and concerts</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Webster_Bank_Arena" title="Webster Bank Arena">Webster Bank Arena</a> – Sporting events venue, but also hosts large concerts</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_festivals_and_concert_series">Music festivals and concert series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music festivals and concert series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bridgeport has been the annual home to <a href="/wiki/Gathering_of_the_Vibes" title="Gathering of the Vibes">Gathering of the Vibes</a>, a weekend long arts, music and camping festival featuring some of the best names in festival talent. In 1999, 2000, and 2007 through 2010, thousands of people have come from all over the world to camp in Seaside Park and enjoy such talent as <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bob_Weir_and_Ratdog" title="Bob Weir and Ratdog">Bob Weir and Ratdog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Banana_Blackout" title="Deep Banana Blackout">Deep Banana Blackout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Les_Claypool" title="Les Claypool">Les Claypool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Dust" title="Assembly of Dust">Assembly of Dust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dirty_Dozen_Brass_Band" title="Dirty Dozen Brass Band">Dirty Dozen Brass Band</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Lobos" title="Los Lobos">Los Lobos</a> and Bridgeport's own <a href="/wiki/The_Alternate_Routes" title="The Alternate Routes">The Alternate Routes</a>.</p>
<p>Since 1945, the Greater Bridgeport Symphony has been a cultural and musical gem for the City of Bridgeport and its surrounding towns, performing at the 1,400 seat Klein Memorial Auditorium. The orchestra has a rich and vibrant history. Under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Meier" title="Gustav Meier">Gustav Meier</a> for the past 41 years, the prestigious orchestra has welcomed international soloists <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Sills" title="Beverly Sills">Beverly Sills</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Midori_Samson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Midori Samson (page does not exist)">Midori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benny_Goodman" title="Benny Goodman">Benny Goodman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itzhak_Perlman" title="Itzhak Perlman">Itzhak Perlman</a> with other links to legends like <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bernstein" title="Leonard Bernstein">Leonard Bernstein</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Iturbi" title="Jose Iturbi">Jose Iturbi</a>. Through its annual Carlson-Horn Competition for Young Instrumentalist created many new bright professional soloists including Andrew Armstrong, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Markov" title="Alexander Markov">Alexander Markov</a>, and Anita Chen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums.2C_zoos_and_parks">Museums, zoos and parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Museums, zoos and parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport has a number of museums, ranging from the science-oriented to fine arts and historical, as well as the state's largest zoo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globe2008_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-globe2008-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Museum_and_Planetarium" title="Discovery Museum and Planetarium">Discovery Museum and Planetarium</a> emphasizes exhibits on science, with the state's only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Challenger_Center" title="Challenger Center">Challenger Center</a>, affiliated with the national space program.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Housatonic_Museum_of_Art" title="Housatonic Museum of Art">Housatonic Museum of Art</a>, located at <a href="/wiki/Housatonic_Community_College" title="Housatonic Community College">Housatonic Community College</a>, has the largest collection of art of any two-year college in the nation.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Barnum_Museum" title="Barnum Museum">Barnum Museum</a> celebrates the showman, circuses and Bridgeport history.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beardsley_Zoo" title="Beardsley Zoo">Beardsley Zoo</a> is the only such center in Connecticut.</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><b>Novels</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Bridgeport is the setting for <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Howard" title="Maureen Howard">Maureen Howard</a>'s <i>Natural History</i>, a novel that includes scenes from the city's history and depicts important historical figures such as <a href="/wiki/P._T._Barnum" title="P. T. Barnum">P. T. Barnum</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">AHL</a>, Ice hockey</td>

<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg"><img alt="Bridgeport Sound Tigers logo.svg" data-file-height="71" data-file-width="78" height="46" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg/50px-Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg/75px-Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg/100px-Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers_logo.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Webster_Bank_Arena" title="Webster Bank Arena">Webster Bank Arena</a> serves as the city's sports and hospitality center. Seating 10,000, the Arena serves as the home rink of the <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Sound_Tigers" title="Bridgeport Sound Tigers">Bridgeport Sound Tigers</a> AHL hockey team and as the home court of <a href="/wiki/Fairfield_University" title="Fairfield University">Fairfield University</a>'s basketball team.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Ballpark_at_Harbor_Yard" title="The Ballpark at Harbor Yard">The Ballpark at Harbor Yard</a> serves as a minor-league baseball stadium, and was built in 1998 to serve as the homefield of the <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Bluefish" title="Bridgeport Bluefish">Bridgeport Bluefish</a>. It is located downtown on a former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brownfield" title="Brownfield">brownfield</a> site. It is visually prominent to commuters on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Connecticut" title="Interstate 95 in Connecticut">I-95</a> or on passing trains.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Stadium_(Bridgeport)" title="John F. Kennedy Stadium (Bridgeport)">Kennedy Stadium</a> serves as a community sports facility. In the late 1960s and early 1970s, it was the home of an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Football_League" title="Atlantic Coast Football League">Atlantic Coast Football League</a> minor league football team, the Bridgeport Jets, a <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> <a href="/wiki/Farm_team" title="Farm team">farm team</a> also known locally as the Hi-Ho Jets due to their sponsorship by the (Hi-Ho) D'Addario construction company.</p>
<p>Fairfield University is located in the neighboring town of <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield, Connecticut">Fairfield</a>, and many of the athletic teams play on campus. Only the men's and women's basketball teams play in Bridgeport.</p>
<p>Nutmeg Curling Club, one of two <a href="/wiki/Curling" title="Curling">curling</a> clubs in Connecticut, is located in Bridgeport. It is the home club of the 2013 USA Mixed National Champions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> led by club members Derek Surka and Charissa Lin. The club is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Curling_Club" title="Grand National Curling Club">Grand National Curling Club</a> Region.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/WCUM" title="WCUM">WCUM</a> AM 1450; 1,000 watts (formerly WJBX-AM, and before that, WNAB-AM) Spanish Format station better known as Radio Cumbre.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WDJZ" title="WDJZ">WDJZ</a> AM 1530; 5,000 watts (daytime only) Gospel Radio that serves the African American and Caribbean communities in the Bridgeport Metro area.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WICC_(AM)" title="WICC (AM)">WICC-AM</a> 600; 1,000 watts (daytime), 500 watts (nighttime) – WICC began broadcasting on November 21, 1926, when a previous radio station, WCWS, was given a new name, WICC. The last three letters standing for Industrial Capitol of Connecticut. The Bridgeport Broadcasting Company Inc. was the new station's owner. Back then, the station was powered at 500 watts. From 1951 to 1956 one of the station's radio hosts was <a href="/wiki/Bob_Crane" title="Bob Crane">Bob Crane</a>, who later went on to play Col. Robert Hogan on the <i>Hogan's Heroes</i> television comedy series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> WICC's transmitter is located on <a href="/wiki/Pleasure_Beach" title="Pleasure Beach">Pleasure Beach</a>, an island located between downtown Bridgeport and Long Island Sound.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WEBE" title="WEBE">WEBE</a>-FM 107.9; 50,000 watts. WEBE108 is "CT's Best Music Variety!" owned and operated by Cumulus Media. Licensed to Westport, CT, with studios and transmitter in Bridgeport.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WEZN-FM" title="WEZN-FM">WEZN-FM</a> 99.9; 27,500 watts (formerly WJZZ-FM). Star 99.9 is "Today's Best Mix!" The station owned by Connoisseur Media. Lincensed to Bridgeport, CT, with studios in Milford and transmitter in Shelton.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WPKN" title="WPKN">WPKN</a>-FM 89.5; 10,000 watts<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Due to Bridgeport's close proximity to Long Island Sound, many radio stations from New York and Long Island are received clearly day and night in the market. These include WMCA, WFAN, WOR, WABC, WNYC, WCBS, WEPN, WQEW, WBLI, and WALK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
