<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Elsolnews.com, a community Spanish language weekly newspaper covering news and events.</li>
<li><i>Connecticut Post</i> - Formerly the <i>Bridgeport Post and Bridgeport Telegram</i>, which covers Bridgeport and the surrounding area. The newspaper is printed daily.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_2">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Broadcasting_Company" title="National Broadcasting Company">NBC's</a> pioneer <a href="/wiki/Ultra_high_frequency" title="Ultra high frequency">UHF TV</a> test site from December 29, 1949 to August 23, 1952;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> the equipment from the <a href="/wiki/KC2XAK" title="KC2XAK">"Operation Bridgeport"</a> tests was later deployed commercially at <a href="/wiki/KPTV" title="KPTV">KPTV</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a> (1952-1957). While Bridgeport is primarily served by <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> stations, some local UHF broadcasters operate today:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Public_Television" title="Connecticut Public Television">WEDW</a> channel 49; one of the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Public_Television" title="Connecticut Public Television">Connecticut Public Television</a> stations, broadcasts from Bridgeport and can be seen in Hartford.</li>
<li>In 2011, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTNH-TV" title="WTNH-TV">WTNH-TV</a> opened a satellite studio in the offices of the Connecticut Post downtown on State Street.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WZME" title="WZME">WZME</a> channel 43 now mostly broadcasts older classic TV shows. Licensed to Bridgeport with transmitter in Trumbull.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_Memorial_Airport" title="Sikorsky Memorial Airport">Sikorsky Memorial Airport</a> in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Stratford,_Connecticut" title="Stratford, Connecticut">Stratford</a> is owned by the city of Bridgeport. It once provided regional flights to major cities, but commercial operations at the airport were terminated in November 1999.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Surface_thoroughfares">Surface thoroughfares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Surface thoroughfares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The main portion of the city is divided by major north/south roads that approximately parallel each other:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Main Street</b>, the city's principal artery, extending from the Trumbull town line down through the North End, under Routes 8/25, and into downtown, with its southern terminus at Seaside Park. The portion North of State Street was laid out as the "Newtown Turnpike" in 1795. Porter Street, Beechmont Avenue, and Kaechele Place are former curves in this highway that were lopped of as the road was straightened in the 19th century.</li>
<li><b>Park Avenue</b> is a main highway that is on the borderline with the town of Fairfield (North of its intersection with Brooklawn Avenue) and extends from the <a href="/wiki/Trumbull,_Connecticut" title="Trumbull, Connecticut">Trumbull, Connecticut</a> border in the North End to the South End at Seaside Park. It was known as "Division Street" until 1867. It is the easternmost of the "11 o'clock" roadways laid out in 17th-century Fairfield (their north-northwesterly direction points them like a clock's hands at that hour, exactly perpendicular to the shoreline of Long Island Sound, that facilitated land distribution).</li>
<li><b>Clinton/Brooklawn Avenues</b> are a central artery through the West End, extending North from Railroad Avenue to the Fairfield line at the Rooster River. The portion to the North of Fairfield Avenue was laid out in the 17th century at the center of the agricultural village of Stratfield. It was known as "Stratfield Road" prior to 1870.</li>
<li><b>Brewster Street</b> extends from Black Rock Harbor North to the Fairfield line at Ash Creek, and is the major north-south artery through the Black Rock neighborhood. This was the southernmost portion of the "Black Rock Turnpike," a toll road of the late-18th century that extended North as far as Danbury.</li>
<li><b>Madison Avenue</b> is situated between Main Street and Park Avenue, that extends from the Trumbull town line in the North End and continues through the West Side. It was formerly known as "Chestnut Hill Road," and follows the route of an Indian path.</li>
<li><b>Reservoir Avenue</b> was part of a turnpike that was laid out in 1817 in an almost arrow-straight line from Bridgeport north to the Monroe Green (it followed Daniels Farm Road in Trumbull and Moose Hill Road in Monroe). The "Reservoir" was a stone structure at the intersection of Sylvan Avenue, to which water was pumped from nearby Bunnell's Pond, and from which water was supplied to the entire city by gravity. Prior to construction of the Route 25-8 Expressway, this street extended South to North Avenue.</li>
<li><b>Noble Avenue</b> extends from the corner of Congress Street just South of Washington Park to the intersection of East Main Street and Huntington Turnpike. The portion below Boston Avenue was laid out in 1850 as "Noble Street;" the part to the north was added to connect with the entrance to the new Beardsley Park in 1878.</li>
<li><b>East Main Street</b> is the major North/South road through East Bridgeport, extending from the Trumbull/Stratford line though the East Side, ending at Bridgeport Harbor. The portion South of Boston Avenue/Old Mill Green was laid out in 1800.</li>
<li><b>Huntington Road/Huntington Turnpike</b> is the major roadway through the Upper East Side, extending Northeasterly from the Berkshire Bridge to the Trumbull town line (a small portion today becomes part of East Main Street). It was one of a number of turnpikes laid out in the immediate post-Revolutionary period to funnel rural commerce to the fledgling city's seaport, and formerly extended to the city center by way of North Washington Avenue.</li>
<li><b>Seaview Avenue</b> runs the length of the East End neighborhood on the East shore of Pembroke Lake, Yellow Mill Pond, and Bridgeport Harbor. It extends Northwesterly from Central to Stratford Avenues, then due North from Stratford to Boston Avenues. It was laid out at the time of the Civil War in three sections that were later connected: "Sea View Avenue" South of Stratford Avenue: "West Avenue" at Deacon's Point, from Sixth Street North to the railroad tracks; and "Lake Avenue," from Barnum Avenue North to Boston Avenue.</li>
<li><b>Central/Palisade Avenues</b> were laid out as farm highways through the westerly portions of what was the town of Stratford in the early 19th century. They form a North-South axis through the center of today's East End. The portion of Central Avenue to the north of Barnum Avenue was known as "Prospect Street" from the 1860s through 1889 due to the vistas from its hillside location.</li>
</ul>
<p>The major East/West roads in the city include Barnum Avenue, Boston Avenue, Fairfield Avenue/Stratford Avenue, North Avenue, Capitol Avenue, State Street, and Railroad Avenue:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Barnum Avenue</b> extends from the Stratford line, below Old Mill Hill, and ends at the Pequonnock River. The portion through the East Side was laid out as "Barnum Street" in 1850. From Pembroke Lake to Mill Hill Avenue was added in 1863. The road from Mill Hill Avenue to the Washington Bridge between Stratford and Milford was laid out as the "Air Line Highway" in 1870.</li>
<li><b>Boston Avenue</b> breaks off from Barnum Avenue near the Bridgeport line in Stratford and travels east-west over Old Mill Hill to the Upper East Side toward the North End. It follows the route of an Indian path, crossing Old Mill Brook and the Pequonnock River and the southernmost points where they were fordable, that became the Post Road in the 1670s.</li>
<li><b>Stratford Avenue</b> starts in the South End of the town of Stratford and travels Southwest through the East End. It then travels East through East Bridgeport directly into the center of Downtown Bridgeport, where it turns into <b>Fairfield Avenue</b> at Water Street. It was laid out in 1795 as a more direct route for the "Post Road," and the bridge built that year over the Pequonnock was the origin of the name "Bridgeport." <b>Connecticut Avenue,</b> which parallels it one block to the North through the East End, is a one-way street heading West, while Stratford Avenue is one-way heading East.</li>
<li><b>Fairfield Avenue</b> extends West and then Southwest through the West End and into Black Rock, where it turns into the Boston Post Road, or simply, the Post Road, at the <a href="/wiki/Fairfield,_Connecticut" title="Fairfield, Connecticut">Fairfield, Connecticut</a> line. Its route through the West End parallels what had been the northerly edge of an extensive salt marsh, and had been in existence in the 18th century. The portion through Black Rock was added in the 1870s.</li>
<li><b>North Avenue</b> begins at Boston Avenue where the East Side abuts the Island Brook neighborhood at the Pequonnock River and extends Southwest diagonally through the city as US 1. It then turns into <b>Kings Highway</b> in Fairfield. As with Boston Avenue, it was follows an Indian trail, and was formalized as a part of the New York-to-Boston Post Road in the 1670s.</li>
<li><b>Capitol Avenue</b> begins by breaking off from North Avenue at Island Brook Avenue Extension. It travels West across the Old North End and Brooklawn neighborhoods and ends at the Fairfield line.</li>
<li><b>State Street</b> begins in Downtown and cuts across the West End, where it terminates (as 'State Street Extension') at the Fairfield line. The portion from Park Avenue to Bridgeport Harbor was in existence by the 1760s; the part to the West of Park Avenue was extended across what was then marshy terrain in 1867.</li>
<li><b>Atlantic Street</b> bisects the South End neighborhood, historically separating the well-to-do residential district that adjoined the old portion of Seaside Park from the working-class blocks to the north. Today it forms the north border of the University of Bridgeport campus.</li>
<li><b>Railroad Avenue</b> extends from Broad Street just below Downtown Bridgeport and runs parallel with the Metro North/New Haven Railroad lines. The Westbound side is to the north of the tracks, and the Eastbound side to the south of them. It terminates at Fairfield Avenue in the West End.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bridgeport has several major roadways. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Connecticut" title="Interstate 95 in Connecticut">Interstate 95</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_8_(Connecticut)" title="Route 8 (Connecticut)">Route 8</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_25_(Connecticut)" title="Route 25 (Connecticut)">Route 25</a> Connector meet in downtown Bridgeport. I-95 runs east-west near the coast heading towards New York City to the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">Providence</a> to the northeast. Routes 8 and 25 run north-south across the city, with the two routes splitting just north of the city. Route 8 continues towards <a href="/wiki/Waterbury,_Connecticut" title="Waterbury, Connecticut">Waterbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torrington,_Connecticut" title="Torrington, Connecticut">Torrington</a> and Route 25 continues towards the <a href="/wiki/Danbury,_Connecticut" title="Danbury, Connecticut">Danbury</a> area. Both Routes 8 and 25 connect to the <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Parkway" title="Merritt Parkway">Merritt Parkway</a> in the adjacent town of <a href="/wiki/Trumbull,_Connecticut" title="Trumbull, Connecticut">Trumbull</a>.</p>
<p>Other major surface arteries are <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Connecticut" title="U.S. Route 1 in Connecticut">U.S. 1</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Post_Road" title="Boston Post Road">Boston Post Road</a>), which runs east-west north of downtown, and Main Street, which runs north-south towards Trumbull center. The city also has several secondary state highways, namely, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_127_(Connecticut)" title="Route 127 (Connecticut)">Route 127</a> (East Main Street), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Route_130_(Connecticut)" title="Route 130 (Connecticut)">Route 130</a> (Connecticut Ave, Stratford Ave, Fairfield Ave and Water Street), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huntington_Turnpike" title="Huntington Turnpike">Huntington Turnpike</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railroad_and_ferries">Railroad and ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Railroad and ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport,_CT_station_eastbound,_December_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg/220px-New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg/330px-New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg/440px-New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport%2C_CT_station_eastbound%2C_December_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Haven_Line_train_approaches_Bridgeport,_CT_station_eastbound,_December_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/New_Haven_Line" title="New Haven Line">New Haven Line</a> train approaches the intermodal transit hub at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridgeport_(Metro-North_station)" title="Bridgeport (Metro-North station)">Bridgeport Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_Traction_Company" title="Bridgeport Traction Company">Bridgeport Traction Company</a> provided streetcar service in the region until 1937. The Housatonic Railroad carried passengers North through the Pequonnock and Housatonic Valleys prior to 1933.</p>
<p>The city is connected to nearby New York City by both <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North</a> commuter trains, which serve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridgeport_(Metro-North_station)" title="Bridgeport (Metro-North station)">Bridgeport's Metro-North station</a>. Many residents commute to New York jobs on these trains, and the city to some extent is developing as an outpost of New York–based workers seeking cheaper rents and larger living spaces. Connecting service is also available to <a href="/wiki/Waterbury,_Connecticut" title="Waterbury, Connecticut">Waterbury</a> via Metro-North, and <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a> via Amtrak and Metro-North. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoreline_East" title="Shoreline East">Shoreline East</a> service links <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Saybrook" title="Old Saybrook">Old Saybrook</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London</a> with New Haven, which extends to Bridgeport and Stamford during weekday rush hours only.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport_%26_Port_Jefferson_Ferry" title="Bridgeport &amp; Port Jefferson Ferry">Bridgeport &amp; Port Jefferson Ferry</a> service runs from Bridgeport across <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a> to <a href="/wiki/Port_Jefferson,_New_York" title="Port Jefferson, New York">Port Jefferson</a>, New York; the three vessels "Grand Republic", "P.T. Barnum" and "Park City" transport both automobiles and passengers.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Bridgeport_Transit_Authority" title="Greater Bridgeport Transit Authority">Greater Bridgeport Transit Authority</a> (GBTA) provides bus service to Bridgeport and its immediate suburbs. Route 2 the Coastal Link goes west to Norwalk and east to Westfield's Connecticut Post Mall in Milford, from where <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Transit" title="Connecticut Transit">Connecticut Transit</a> can bring passengers to the New Haven Green. <a href="/wiki/Greyhound" title="Greyhound">Greyhound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan_Bus_Lines" title="Peter Pan Bus Lines">Peter Pan Bus Lines</a> both offer intercity bus service to points throughout the Northeast and points beyond.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sites">Historic sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Historic sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_districts">Historic districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bridgeport,_Connecticut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Historic districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bridgeport has five local historic districts, where exterior changes to structures are under the control of two Historic District Commissions:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Black Rock Harbor Historic District</b>, 88 buildings along Ellsworth, Brewster, and Beacon Streets, includes the village center of a historic seaport, with buildings that date back to the 17th century</li>
<li><b>Pembroke City Historic District</b>, 266 buildings in a general two-block radius of Washington Park, a planned residential development constructed 1850-1900 that contains the city's most important concentration of Victorian architecture</li>
<li><b>Stratfield Historic District</b>, 300 buildings along Clinton, Brooklawn, and Laurel Avenues that made up an elite residential district of the Edwardian era</li>
<li><b>Barnum-Palliser Development Historic District</b>, 33 buildings on Austin, Gregory, and Atlantic Streets and Myrtle Avenue that was a planned working-class development of the 1880s designed by the architectural firm of Palliser, Palliser, and Company</li>
<li><b>Marina Park Historic District</b>, 14 buildings along South Park Avenue and Marina Park, contains some of the city's most opulent late 19th-early 20th century mansions overlooking Seaside Park</li>
</ul>

<li><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFEB1911">"<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica/Bridgeport" title="s:1911 Encyclopædia Britannica/Bridgeport">Bridgeport</a>", <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="s:1911 Encyclopædia Britannica"><i>Encyclopædia Britannica</i>, 11th ed.</a>, <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica/Volume_III" title="s:1911 Encyclopædia Britannica/Volume III">Vol. III</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambridge,_England" title="Cambridge, England">Cambridge</a>: Cambridge University Press, 1911, p. 532</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABridgeport%2C+Connecticut&amp;rft.atitle=Bridgeport&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclop%C3%A6dia+Britannica%2C+11th+ed.%2C+Vol.+III&amp;rft.date=1911&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.pages=532&amp;rft.place=Cambridge&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFBucki2001">Bucki, Cecelia Bucki (2001), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=5sqULah9Jj0C&amp;printsec=frontcover" rel="nofollow"><i>Bridgeport's Socialist New Deal, 1915–36</i></a>, University of Illinois Press, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-252-02687-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-252-02687-4">978-0-252-02687-4</a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABridgeport%2C+Connecticut&amp;rft.aufirst=Cecelia+Bucki&amp;rft.aulast=Bucki&amp;rft.btitle=Bridgeport%27s+Socialist+New+Deal%2C+1915%9336&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3D5sqULah9Jj0C%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-252-02687-4&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Illinois+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFNolen1916">Nolen, John (1916), <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=s9sAAAAAYAAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover" rel="nofollow"><i>Better City Planning For Bridgeport</i></a>, Bridgeport: City Plan Commission</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABridgeport%2C+Connecticut&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.aulast=Nolen&amp;rft.btitle=Better+City+Planning+For+Bridgeport&amp;rft.date=1916&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3Ds9sAAAAAYAAJ%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rft.place=Bridgeport&amp;rft.pub=City+Plan+Commission&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>.</li>
<li><cite class="citation" id="CITEREFOrcutt1886">Orcutt, Samuel (1886), <i>A History of the Old Town of Stratford and City of Bridgeport Connecticut</i>, <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/historyofoldtown01orcu#page/n5/mode/2up" rel="nofollow">Vol. I</a> &amp; <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/ahistoryoldtown01conngoog#page/n5/mode/2up" rel="nofollow">II</a>, Bridgeport: Fairfield County Historical Society</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABridgeport%2C+Connecticut&amp;rft.aufirst=Samuel&amp;rft.aulast=Orcutt&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+the+Old+Town+of+Stratford+and+City+of+Bridgeport+Connecticut&amp;rft.date=1886&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Bridgeport&amp;rft.pub=Fairfield+County+Historical+Society&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span>.</li>
